<a id="tabsdata.AzureDestination.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L610">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
    *results,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data to local parquet chunks. This method will
receive the resulting data from the user function and must store it in
the local system as parquet files, using the working_dir. Note: This
method should *not* materialize the data, it should only store it in the
local system.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A list of the intermediate files created

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.AzureDestination.stream"></a>
<ResponseField name="stream" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L596">

```python
def stream(
    working_dir: str,
    *results,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data. This method will receive the resulting data
from the user function and must store it in the desired location.
Note: this method *might* materialize the data provided in a single chunk
generated by the chunk function if invoked, so chunks should be of an
appropriate size.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any intermediate files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** None

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L420" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>

<a id="tabsdata.AzureSource.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/file_inputs.py#L318">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
)
```

Trigger the import of the data. This must be implemented in any class that
inherits from this class unless directly implementing streaming. The method will
receive a folder where it must store the data as parquet files, and return a
list of the paths of the files created. This files will then be loaded and
mapped to the dataset function in positional order, so if you want file.parquet
to be the first argument of the dataset function, you must return it first. If
you want a parameter to receive multiple files, return a list of the paths. For
example, you would give the following return to provide a first argument with a
single file and a second argument with two files:return
[“file1.parquet”, [“file2.parquet”, “file3.parquet”]]

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir (str)">
  The folder where the files must be stored
</ParamField>

**Returns:** The path of the file(s) created, inthe order they must be mapped to the dataset function

**Returns:** Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/file_inputs.py#L88" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>
</div>

  <a id="tabsdata.CSVFormat"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>CSVFormat</summary>

```python
class CSVFormat(
    separator: str | int = ',',
    quote_char: str | int = '"',
    eol_char: str | int = '\n',
    input_encoding: str = 'Utf8',
    input_null_values: list | None = None,
    input_missing_is_null: bool = True,
    input_truncate_ragged_lines: bool = False,
    input_comment_prefix: str | int | None = None,
    input_try_parse_dates: bool = False,
    input_decimal_comma: bool = False,
    input_has_header: bool = True,
    input_skip_rows: int = 0,
    input_skip_rows_after_header: int = 0,
    input_raise_if_empty: bool = True,
    input_ignore_errors: bool = False,
    output_include_header: bool = True,
    output_datetime_format: str | None = None,
    output_date_format: str | None = None,
    output_time_format: str | None = None,
    output_float_scientific: bool | None = None,
    output_float_precision: int | None = None,
    output_null_value: str | None = None,
    output_quote_style: str | None = None,
    output_maintain_order: bool = True,
)
```

Bases: `FileFormat`

CSV file format.

**Categories:** file-format

<ResponseField name="separator" type="str" kind="variable">
  The separator of the CSV file.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="quote_char" type="str" kind="variable">
  The quote character of the CSV file.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="eol_char" type="str" kind="variable">
  The end of line character of the CSV file.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_encoding" type="str" kind="variable">
  The encoding of the CSV file. Only used when importing
data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_null_values" type="list" kind="variable">
  The null values of the CSV file. Only used
when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_missing_is_null" type="bool" kind="variable">
  Whether missing values should be marked as null.
Only used when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_truncate_ragged_lines" type="bool" kind="variable">
  Whether to truncate ragged lines of the
CSV file. Only used when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_comment_prefix" type="str" kind="variable">
  The comment prefix of the CSV file.
Only used when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_try_parse_dates" type="bool" kind="variable">
  Whether to try parse dates of the CSV file. Only
used when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_decimal_comma" type="bool" kind="variable">
  Whether the CSV file uses decimal comma. Only used
when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_has_header" type="bool" kind="variable">
  If the CSV file has header. Only used when importing
data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_skip_rows" type="int" kind="variable">
  How many rows should be skipped in the CSV file. Only
used when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_skip_rows_after_header" type="int" kind="variable">
  How many rows should be skipped after the
header in the CSV file. Only used when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_raise_if_empty" type="bool" kind="variable">
  If an error should be raised for an empty CSV. Only
used when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="input_ignore_errors" type="bool" kind="variable">
  If the errors loading the CSV must be ignored. Only
used when importing data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_include_header" type="bool" kind="variable">
  Whether to include header in the CSV
output. Only used when exporting data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_datetime_format" type="str" kind="variable">
  A format string, with the
specifiers defined by the chrono Rust crate. If no format specified,
the default fractional-second precision is inferred from the maximum
timeunit found in the frame’s Datetime cols (if any). Only used when
exporting data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_date_format" type="str" kind="variable">
  A format string, with the specifiers
defined by the chrono Rust crate. Only used when exporting data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_time_format" type="str" kind="variable">
  A format string, with the specifiers
defined by the chrono Rust crate. Only used when exporting data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_float_scientific" type="bool" kind="variable">
  Whether to use scientific form
always (true), never (false), or automatically (None). Only used when
exporting data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_float_precision" type="int" kind="variable">
  Number of decimal places to write.
Only used when exporting data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_null_value" type="str" kind="variable">
  A string representing null values
(defaulting to the empty string). Only used when exporting data.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_quote_style" type="str" kind="variable">
  Determines the quoting strategy used.
Only used when exporting data.
* necessary (default): This puts quotes around fields only when
necessary. They are necessary when fields contain a quote, separator
or record terminator. Quotes are also necessary when writing an empty
record (which is indistinguishable from a record with one empty field).
This is the default.
* always: This puts quotes around every field. Always.
* never: This never puts quotes around fields, even if that results
in invalid CSV data (e.g.: by not quoting strings containing the
separator).
* non_numeric: This puts quotes around all fields that are
non-numeric. Namely, when writing a field that does not parse as a
valid float or integer, then quotes will be used even if they aren`t
strictly necessary.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="output_maintain_order" type="bool" kind="variable">
  Maintain the order in which data is
processed. Setting this to False will be slightly faster. Only used
when exporting data.
</ResponseField>

</details>

Base StageTrigger for Change Data Capture (CDC) connectors.

logic for all CDC connectors. Database-specific subclasses implement the
ingestion details for their respective replication protocols.

```python
def run(
    context: StageTriggerContext,
)
```

Continuously runs the stage trigger logic using the received context to
trigger and monitor executions.
SUCCESS if the StageTrigger.end datetime is reached. exit with 0.
ERROR if any issue stops it from working or recovering. exit with 1.
STOPPED upon a signal. exit with 0.

    <a id="tabsdata.ClickHouseConn"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>ClickHouseConn</summary>

```python
class ClickHouseConn(
    **kwargs,
)
```

Bases: Conn

Represents a connection configuration for ClickHouse with cloud-staged bulk
loading.

ClickHouse ingests data via cloud storage (S3, Azure Blob, or GCS): files are
first uploaded to the configured staging area and then loaded into ClickHouse
using the matching table function (`s3()`, `azureBlobStorage()`, or
`s3()` pointed at GCS).

<a id="tabsdata.ClickHouseConn.credentials"></a>
<ResponseField name="credentials" kind="property">
The credentials used to authenticate with ClickHouse.  `None` if no
credentials were provided (ClickHouse `default` user, no password).
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.ClickHouseConn.cx_dst_configs_clickhouse"></a>
<ResponseField name="cx_dst_configs_clickhouse" kind="property">
Destination-specific configuration parameters for the ClickHouse connection.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.ClickHouseConn.cx_src_configs_clickhouse"></a>
<ResponseField name="cx_src_configs_clickhouse" kind="property">
Source-specific configuration parameters for the ClickHouse connection.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.ClickHouseConn.database"></a>
<ResponseField name="database" kind="property">
The target ClickHouse database name.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.ClickHouseConn.enforce_connection_params"></a>
<ResponseField name="enforce_connection_params" kind="property">
Whether to enforce connection parameters for the ClickHouse connection.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.ClickHouseConn.host"></a>
<ResponseField name="host" kind="property">
The ClickHouse server hostname or IP address.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.ClickHouseConn.port"></a>
<ResponseField name="port" kind="property">
The HTTP(S) port of the ClickHouse server.

Bases: DestinationPlugin

Destination plugin for writing data to ClickHouse using cloud-staged bulk loading.

Data is first written as Parquet files to the configured cloud storage staging area
(S3, Azure Blob, or GCS) and then ingested into ClickHouse via its native table
functions (`s3()`, `azureBlobStorage()`).

 <a id="tabsdata.CronTrigger"></a>

<summary>CronTrigger</summary>

```python
class CronTrigger(
    mask: str,
    start: datetime | None = None,
    end: datetime | None = None,
)
```

Bases: [object](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#object)

Represents a cron-based trigger for scheduling Tabsdata publishers,
subscribers and transformers.

This class defines a trigger based on a cron expression, with optional
start and end times to constrain its activation period. It validates the
cron mask and time boundaries to ensure the trigger is well-formed.

**Categories:** trigger

<a id="tabsdata.CronTrigger.end"></a>
<ResponseField name="end" kind="property">
Gets the end time of the trigger as a timezone-aware ISO 8601 string
with ‘Z’ timezone.

 **Returns:** The end time in ISO format, or None if not set.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.CronTrigger.mask"></a>
<ResponseField name="mask" kind="property">
Gets the cron expression mask.

 **Returns:** The cron expression string.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.CronTrigger.start"></a>
<ResponseField name="start" kind="property">
Gets the start time of the trigger as a timezone-aware ISO 8601 string
with ‘Z’ timezone.

 **Returns:** The start time in ISO format, or None if not set.
</ResponseField>

</details>

<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-databricks/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/databricks/_connector.py#L750">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
    *results: LazyFrame | None,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data to local parquet chunks. This method will
receive the resulting data from the user function and must store it in
the local system as parquet files, using the working_dir. Note: This
method should *not* materialize the data, it should only store it in the
local system.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A list of the intermediate files created

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DatabricksDestination.stream"></a>
<ResponseField name="stream" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-databricks/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/databricks/_connector.py#L734">

```python
def stream(
    working_dir: str,
    *results: List[LazyFrame | None] | LazyFrame | None,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data. This method will receive the resulting data
from the user function and must store it in the desired location.
Note: this method *might* materialize the data provided in a single chunk
generated by the chunk function if invoked, so chunks should be of an
appropriate size.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any intermediate files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** None

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DatabricksDestination.write"></a>

```python
)
```

    <a id="tabsdata.DatabricksSource"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>DatabricksSource</summary>

```python
class DatabricksSource(
    host_url: str,
    token: str | Secret,
    queries: list[str] | str,
    initial_values: dict | None = None,
    warehouse: str | None = None,
    warehouse_id: str | None = None,
    **kwargs,
)
```

Bases: SourcePlugin

Databricks based data inputs.

**Categories:** source

<a id="tabsdata.DatabricksSource.host_url"></a>
<ResponseField name="host_url" kind="property">

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DatabricksSource.initial_values"></a>
<ResponseField name="initial_values" kind="property">
The initial values for the parameters in the SQL queries.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DatabricksSource.queries"></a>
<ResponseField name="queries" kind="property">

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DatabricksSource.token"></a>
<ResponseField name="token" kind="property">

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DatabricksSource.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-databricks/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/databricks/_connector.py#L254">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
)
```

Trigger the import of the data. This must be implemented in any class that
inherits from this class unless directly implementing streaming. The method will
receive a folder where it must store the data as parquet files, and return a
list of the paths of the files created. This files will then be loaded and
mapped to the dataset function in positional order, so if you want file.parquet
to be the first argument of the dataset function, you must return it first. If
you want a parameter to receive multiple files, return a list of the paths. For
example, you would give the following return to provide a first argument with a
single file and a second argument with two files:return
[“file1.parquet”, [“file2.parquet”, “file3.parquet”]]

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir (str)">
  The folder where the files must be stored
</ParamField>

**Returns:** The path of the file(s) created, inthe order they must be mapped to the dataset function

**Returns:** Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]

</ResponseField>

</details>

Bases: CdcTrigger

A CdcTrigger that captures changes from a Db2 database using SQL Replication.

This trigger connects to a Db2 server, reads change data capture events (inserts,
updates, deletes) on specified tables via SQL Replication, and stages them.

  <a id="tabsdata.DestinationPlugin"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>DestinationPlugin</summary>

```python
class DestinationPlugin()
```

Bases: [object](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#object)

Parent class for subscriber connectors.

  trigger_output(working_dir, `*args`, `**kwargs`):Trigger the exporting of the data. This function will
receive the resulting data from the dataset function
and must store it in the desired location.

**Categories:** plugin

<a id="tabsdata.DestinationPlugin.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/plugin.py#L404">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
    *results: VALID_PLUGIN_RESULT,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data to local parquet chunks. This method will
receive the resulting data from the user function and must store it in
the local system as parquet files, using the working_dir. Note: This
method should *not* materialize the data, it should only store it in the
local system.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A list of the intermediate files created

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DestinationPlugin.stream"></a>
<ResponseField name="stream" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/plugin.py#L384">

```python
def stream(
    working_dir: str,
    *results: VALID_PLUGIN_RESULT,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data. This method will receive the resulting data
from the user function and must store it in the desired location.
Note: this method *might* materialize the data provided in a single chunk
generated by the chunk function if invoked, so chunks should be of an
appropriate size.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any intermediate files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** None

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DestinationPlugin.write"></a>
<ResponseField name="write" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/plugin.py#L429">

```python
def write(
    files: List[str | List[str] | List[List[str]]],
)
```

Given a file or a list of files, write to the desired destination. Note: this
method *might* materialize the data in the files it receives, so chunks
should be of an appropriate size.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="files (str)">
  The file or files to be stored in the final destination.
</ParamField>

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/plugin.py#L298" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>

    <a id="tabsdata.DruidConn"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>DruidConn</summary>

```python
class DruidConn(
    **kwargs,
)
```

Bases: Conn

Represents a connection configuration for Apache Druid with cloud-staged
bulk loading.

Data is first uploaded to the configured cloud staging area (S3, Azure
Blob, or GCS) and then ingested into Druid via the Overlord REST API
using a native batch `index_parallel` ingestion task.

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.credentials"></a>
<ResponseField name="credentials" kind="property">
The credentials used for HTTP Basic authentication.  `None` if no
credentials were provided.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.http_timeout_sec"></a>
<ResponseField name="http_timeout_sec" kind="property">
Timeout in seconds for HTTP requests to the Overlord API.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.max_concurrent_subtasks"></a>
<ResponseField name="max_concurrent_subtasks" kind="property">
Maximum number of parallel sub-tasks inside the ingestion task.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.max_rows_in_memory"></a>
<ResponseField name="max_rows_in_memory" kind="property">
In-memory buffer size during ingestion.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.max_rows_per_segment"></a>
<ResponseField name="max_rows_per_segment" kind="property">
Maximum number of rows per segment (dynamic partitioning threshold).
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.overlord_url"></a>
<ResponseField name="overlord_url" kind="property">
The base URL of the Druid Overlord REST API.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.segment_granularity"></a>
<ResponseField name="segment_granularity" kind="property">
Time-based partitioning granularity for new segments.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.staging"></a>
<ResponseField name="staging" kind="property">
The cloud storage staging configuration (S3Config, AzureConfig, or
GCSConfig).
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.DruidConn.time_column"></a>
<ResponseField name="time_column" kind="property">
The PyArrow column to use as Druid’s `__time` primary timestamp.
`None` if a constant value should be used.
</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/connections/druid_connection.py#L27" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>

```python
class DruidDest(

)
```

Bases: DestinationPlugin

Destination plugin for writing data to Apache Druid using cloud-staged
bulk loading.

Data is first written as Parquet files to the configured cloud storage
staging area (S3, Azure Blob, or GCS) and then ingested into Druid via
a native batch `index_parallel` task submitted to the Overlord REST API.

**Categories:** destination

```python
    working_dir: str,
    *results: list[LazyFrame | None],
)
```

the cloud staging area.

datasource, in the same order as destination_tables.
</ParamField>

</ResponseField>

```python
)
```

</ParamField>

</ParamField>

  Optional HMACCredentials
carrying GCS HMAC access key and secret for S3-compatible access.
When None, the storage backend operates without explicit
credentials (suitable for public buckets or server-side IAM).
</ParamField>

<a id="tabsdata.GCSSource.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/file_inputs.py#L566">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
)
```

Trigger the import of the data. This must be implemented in any class that
inherits from this class unless directly implementing streaming. The method will
receive a folder where it must store the data as parquet files, and return a
list of the paths of the files created. This files will then be loaded and
mapped to the dataset function in positional order, so if you want file.parquet
to be the first argument of the dataset function, you must return it first. If
you want a parameter to receive multiple files, return a list of the paths. For
example, you would give the following return to provide a first argument with a
single file and a second argument with two files:return
[“file1.parquet”, [“file2.parquet”, “file3.parquet”]]

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir (str)">
  The folder where the files must be stored
</ParamField>

**Returns:** The path of the file(s) created, inthe order they must be mapped to the dataset function

**Returns:** Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/file_inputs.py#L337" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>
</div>

  <a id="tabsdata.HMACCredentials"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>HMACCredentials</summary>

```python
class HMACCredentials(
    access_key: str | Secret,
    secret_key: str | Secret,
)
```

Bases: `Credentials`

Generic HMAC credentials consisting of an access key and a secret key.

These credentials follow the same shape as AWS S3 access keys and are
compatible with any service that uses HMAC-based authentication over the
S3-compatible API, such as GCS HMAC keys or MinIO credentials.

**Categories:** credentials

<ResponseField name="access_key" type="Secret" kind="variable">
  The HMAC access key id.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="secret_key" type="Secret" kind="variable">
  The HMAC secret key.
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="dict" type="to_dict" kind="variable">
  Convert the HMACCredentials object to a dictionary.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.HMACCredentials.access_key"></a>
<ResponseField name="access_key" kind="property">
The HMAC access key id.

 **Type:** Secret
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.HMACCredentials.secret_key"></a>
<ResponseField name="secret_key" kind="property">
The HMAC secret key.

 **Type:** Secret
</ResponseField>

</details>

 <a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>KafkaTrigger</summary>

```python
class KafkaTrigger(
    **kwargs,
)
```

Bases: StageTrigger

A StageTrigger that consumes messages from a Kafka topic and stages them.

This trigger connects to a Kafka cluster, consumes messages from a specified
topic, and uses rollover conditions (time, size, and message count) to
buffer and stage the data.

**Categories:** trigger

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.conn"></a>
<ResponseField name="conn" kind="property">
Kafka consumer connection configuration.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.data_format"></a>

Data format of the messages (“avro”, “json”, “protobuf”).
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.dlq_topic"></a>
<ResponseField name="dlq_topic" kind="property">
Dead-letter queue topic.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.group_id"></a>
<ResponseField name="group_id" kind="property">
Kafka consumer group ID.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.messages_rollover"></a>
<ResponseField name="messages_rollover" kind="property">
Message count-based rollover configuration.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.schema"></a>
<ResponseField name="schema" kind="property">
Schema string for deserializing messages.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.size_rollover_mb"></a>
<ResponseField name="size_rollover_mb" kind="property">
Size-based rollover configuration. Size is specified in megabytes.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.time_rollover_secs"></a>
<ResponseField name="time_rollover_secs" kind="property">
Timeout in seconds for consuming each message.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.KafkaTrigger.topic"></a>
<ResponseField name="topic" kind="property">
Kafka topic to consume from.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.LocalFileDestination.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L988">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
    *results,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data to local parquet chunks. This method will
receive the resulting data from the user function and must store it in
the local system as parquet files, using the working_dir. Note: This
method should *not* materialize the data, it should only store it in the
local system.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A list of the intermediate files created

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.LocalFileDestination.stream"></a>
<ResponseField name="stream" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L975">

```python
def stream(
    working_dir: str,
    *results,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data. This method will receive the resulting data
from the user function and must store it in the desired location.
Note: this method *might* materialize the data provided in a single chunk
generated by the chunk function if invoked, so chunks should be of an
appropriate size.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any intermediate files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** None

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L830" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>

   <a id="tabsdata.MariaDBSource"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">

<summary>MariaDBSource</summary>

```python

    **kwargs,
)
```

Bases: SourcePlugin

MariaDB-based data inputs.

**Categories:** source

<a id="tabsdata.MariaDBSource.credentials"></a>

MariaDB. If no credentials were provided, it will return None.

 **Type:** UserPasswordCredentials | None

 **Type:** dict
</ResponseField>

<ResponseField name="query" kind="property">
The SQL query(s) to execute.

 **Type:** str | List[str]
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.MariaDBSource.uri"></a>
<ResponseField name="uri" kind="property">
The URI of the database where the data is located.

 **Type:** str
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.MariaDBSource.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/sql_inputs.py#L206">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
)
```

Trigger the import of the data. This must be implemented in any class that
inherits from this class unless directly implementing streaming. The method will
receive a folder where it must store the data as parquet files, and return a
list of the paths of the files created. This files will then be loaded and
mapped to the dataset function in positional order, so if you want file.parquet
to be the first argument of the dataset function, you must return it first. If
you want a parameter to receive multiple files, return a list of the paths. For
example, you would give the following return to provide a first argument with a
single file and a second argument with two files:return
[“file1.parquet”, [“file2.parquet”, “file3.parquet”]]

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir (str)">
  The folder where the files must be stored
</ParamField>

**Returns:** The path of the file(s) created, inthe order they must be mapped to the dataset function

**Returns:** Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/sql_inputs.py#L51" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>
</div>

<a id="tabsdata.MongoDBDestination.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-mongodb/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/mongodb/_connector.py#L312">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
    *results: LazyFrame | None,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data to local parquet chunks. This method will
receive the resulting data from the user function and must store it in
the local system as parquet files, using the working_dir. Note: This
method should *not* materialize the data, it should only store it in the
local system.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A list of the intermediate files created

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.MongoDBDestination.stream"></a>
<ResponseField name="stream" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-mongodb/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/mongodb/_connector.py#L271">

```python
def stream(
    working_dir: str,
    *results: List[LazyFrame | None] | LazyFrame | None,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data. This method will receive the resulting data
from the user function and must store it in the desired location.
Note: this method *might* materialize the data provided in a single chunk
generated by the chunk function if invoked, so chunks should be of an
appropriate size.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any intermediate files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** None

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.MongoDBDestination.write"></a>
<ResponseField name="write" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-mongodb/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/mongodb/_connector.py#L214">

```python
def write(
    files,
)
```

This method is used to write the files to the database. It is called
from the stream method, and it is not intended to be called directly.

</ResponseField>

</details>

 <a id="tabsdata.MySQLCdcTrigger"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>MySQLCdcTrigger</summary>

```python
class MySQLCdcTrigger(
    **kwargs,
)
```

Bases: CdcTrigger

A CdcTrigger that captures changes from a MySQL database using binlog replication.

This trigger connects to a MySQL server, reads the binary log for change data
capture events (inserts, updates, deletes) on specified tables, and stages them.

**Categories:** trigger

<a id="tabsdata.MySQLCdcTrigger.blocking_timeout_seconds"></a>
<ResponseField name="blocking_timeout_seconds" kind="property">
Timeout in seconds for blocking reads from the binlog stream.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.MySQLCdcTrigger.server_id"></a>
<ResponseField name="server_id" kind="property">
MySQL server ID for binlog replication.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.MySQLCdcTrigger.start_from"></a>
<ResponseField name="start_from" kind="property">
Position to start reading changes from.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.MySQLCdcTrigger.collect_tables"></a>
<ResponseField name="collect_tables" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-cdc-mysql/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/cdc/mysql/_connector.py#L175">

<ResponseField name="uri" kind="property">

 **Type:** str

<a id="tabsdata.MySQLSource.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/sql_inputs.py#L376">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
)
```

Trigger the import of the data. This must be implemented in any class that
inherits from this class unless directly implementing streaming. The method will
receive a folder where it must store the data as parquet files, and return a
list of the paths of the files created. This files will then be loaded and
mapped to the dataset function in positional order, so if you want file.parquet
to be the first argument of the dataset function, you must return it first. If
you want a parameter to receive multiple files, return a list of the paths. For
example, you would give the following return to provide a first argument with a
single file and a second argument with two files:return
[“file1.parquet”, [“file2.parquet”, “file3.parquet”]]

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir (str)">
  The folder where the files must be stored
</ParamField>

**Returns:** The path of the file(s) created, inthe order they must be mapped to the dataset function

**Returns:** Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/sql_inputs.py#L222" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>
</div>

 <a id="tabsdata.PostgresCdcTrigger"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>PostgresCdcTrigger</summary>

```python
class PostgresCdcTrigger(
    **kwargs,
)
```

Bases: CdcTrigger

A CdcTrigger that captures changes from a PostgreSQL database using WAL
logical replication.

This trigger connects to a PostgreSQL server, reads the write-ahead log via
the wal2json output plugin for change data capture events (inserts, updates,
deletes) on specified tables, and stages them.

**Categories:** trigger

<a id="tabsdata.PostgresCdcTrigger.blocking_timeout_seconds"></a>
<ResponseField name="blocking_timeout_seconds" kind="property">
Timeout in seconds for blocking reads from the replication stream.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.PostgresCdcTrigger.publication_name"></a>
<ResponseField name="publication_name" kind="property">
Name of the PostgreSQL publication to subscribe to.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.PostgresCdcTrigger.replication_slot"></a>
<ResponseField name="replication_slot" kind="property">
Name of the logical replication slot.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.PostgresCdcTrigger.slot_behavior"></a>
<ResponseField name="slot_behavior" kind="property">
Whether to create a new replication slot or reuse an existing one.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.PostgresCdcTrigger.start_from"></a>
<ResponseField name="start_from" kind="property">
Position to start reading changes from.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.PostgresCdcTrigger.collect_tables"></a>
<ResponseField name="collect_tables" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-cdc-postgres/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/cdc/postgres/_connector.py#L207">

```python
def collect_tables(
    session: Any,
    cdc_format: CdcFormat = CdcFormat(values_format='columns', flatten_values=True),
)
```

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.PostgresCdcTrigger.harvest_tables"></a>
<ResponseField name="harvest_tables" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-cdc-postgres/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/cdc/postgres/_connector.py#L214">

```python
def harvest_tables(
    session: Any,
    cdc_format: CdcFormat = CdcFormat(values_format='columns', flatten_values=True),
```


Bases: SourcePlugin

**Categories:** source

<a id="tabsdata.PostgresSource.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/sql_inputs.py#L715">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
)
```

Trigger the import of the data. This must be implemented in any class that
inherits from this class unless directly implementing streaming. The method will
receive a folder where it must store the data as parquet files, and return a
list of the paths of the files created. This files will then be loaded and
mapped to the dataset function in positional order, so if you want file.parquet
to be the first argument of the dataset function, you must return it first. If
you want a parameter to receive multiple files, return a list of the paths. For
example, you would give the following return to provide a first argument with a
single file and a second argument with two files:return
[“file1.parquet”, [“file2.parquet”, “file3.parquet”]]

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir (str)">
  The folder where the files must be stored
</ParamField>

**Returns:** The path of the file(s) created, inthe order they must be mapped to the dataset function

**Returns:** Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/inputs/sql_inputs.py#L560" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>
</div>

<a id="tabsdata.S3Destination.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L1261">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
    *results,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data to local parquet chunks. This method will
receive the resulting data from the user function and must store it in
the local system as parquet files, using the working_dir. Note: This
method should *not* materialize the data, it should only store it in the
local system.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A list of the intermediate files created

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.S3Destination.stream"></a>
<ResponseField name="stream" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L1246">

```python
def stream(
    working_dir: str,
    *results,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data. This method will receive the resulting data
from the user function and must store it in the desired location.
Note: this method *might* materialize the data provided in a single chunk
generated by the chunk function if invoked, so chunks should be of an
appropriate size.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any intermediate files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** None

</ResponseField>

</details>
<a class="entry-source-link" href="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/_io/outputs/file_outputs.py#L1005" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">View source ↗</a>

```python
def chunk(
```

Trigger the import of the data. This must be implemented in any class that
inherits from this class unless directly implementing streaming. The method will
receive a folder where it must store the data as parquet files, and return a
list of the paths of the files created. This files will then be loaded and
mapped to the dataset function in positional order, so if you want file.parquet
to be the first argument of the dataset function, you must return it first. If
you want a parameter to receive multiple files, return a list of the paths. For
example, you would give the following return to provide a first argument with a
single file and a second argument with two files:return
[“file1.parquet”, [“file2.parquet”, “file3.parquet”]]

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir (str)">
  The folder where the files must be stored
</ParamField>

**Returns:** The path of the file(s) created, inthe order they must be mapped to the dataset function

**Returns:** Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]

<summary>SalesforceReportSource</summary>

```python
class SalesforceReportSource(
    credentials: SalesforceCredentials,
    report: str | list[str],
    column_name_strategy: Literal['columnName', 'label'],
    find_report_by: Literal['id', 'name'] = None,
    filter: tuple[str, str, str] | list[tuple[str, str, str]] = None,
    filter_logic: str = None,
    instance_url: str = None,
    last_modified_column: str = None,
    initial_last_modified: str = None,
    **kwargs,
)
```

<a id="tabsdata.SalesforceReportSource.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-salesforce/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/salesforce/_connector.py#L634">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
)
```

Trigger the import of the data. This must be implemented in any class that
inherits from this class unless directly implementing streaming. The method will
receive a folder where it must store the data as parquet files, and return a
list of the paths of the files created. This files will then be loaded and
mapped to the dataset function in positional order, so if you want file.parquet
to be the first argument of the dataset function, you must return it first. If
you want a parameter to receive multiple files, return a list of the paths. For
example, you would give the following return to provide a first argument with a
single file and a second argument with two files:return
[“file1.parquet”, [“file2.parquet”, “file3.parquet”]]

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir (str)">
  The folder where the files must be stored
</ParamField>

**Returns:** The path of the file(s) created, inthe order they must be mapped to the dataset function

**Returns:** Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]

</ResponseField>

</details>

<a id="tabsdata.SnowflakeDestination.chunk"></a>
<ResponseField name="chunk" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-snowflake/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/snowflake/_connector.py#L349">

```python
def chunk(
    working_dir: str,
    *results: LazyFrame | None,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data to local parquet chunks. This method will
receive the resulting data from the user function and must store it in
the local system as parquet files, using the working_dir. Note: This
method should *not* materialize the data, it should only store it in the
local system.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A list of the intermediate files created

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.SnowflakeDestination.stream"></a>
<ResponseField name="stream" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-snowflake/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/snowflake/_connector.py#L330">

```python
def stream(
    working_dir: str,
    *results: List[LazyFrame | None] | LazyFrame | None,
)
```

Trigger the exporting of the data. This method will receive the resulting data
from the user function and must store it in the desired location.
Note: this method *might* materialize the data provided in a single chunk
generated by the chunk function if invoked, so chunks should be of an
appropriate size.

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="working_dir" type="str">
  The folder where any intermediate files generated must
be stored (this refers to temporary files that will be deleted after
the execution of the plugin, not the final destination of the data)
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="results">
  The data to be exported. It is a list of polars LazyFrames or None.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** None

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.SnowflakeDestination.write"></a>
<ResponseField name="write" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/connectors/python/tabsdata-snowflake/src/main/python/tabsdata/connector/snowflake/_connector.py#L186">

```python
def write(
    files,
)
```

This method is used to write the files to the database. It is called

</ResponseField>

  def chunk(working_dir) -&gt; Union[str, Tuple[str, …], List[str]]Trigger the import of the data. The method will receive a folder where it

  <a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn"></a>
<div class="api-entry-wrap">
<details open>
<summary>StarRocksConn</summary>

```python
class StarRocksConn(
    **kwargs,
)
```

Bases: Conn

Represents a connection configuration for StarRocks with cloud-staged bulk
loading.

StarRocks ingests data via cloud storage (S3, Azure Blob, or GCS): files are
first uploaded to the configured staging area and then loaded into StarRocks
using the `FILES()` table function in an `INSERT INTO … SELECT * FROM
FILES(...)` statement.

<a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn.credentials"></a>
<ResponseField name="credentials" kind="property">
The credentials used to authenticate with StarRocks.  `None` if no
credentials were provided (StarRocks `root` user, no password).
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn.cx_dst_configs_starrocks"></a>
<ResponseField name="cx_dst_configs_starrocks" kind="property">
Destination-specific configuration parameters for the StarRocks connection.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn.cx_src_configs_starrocks"></a>
<ResponseField name="cx_src_configs_starrocks" kind="property">
Source-specific configuration parameters for the StarRocks connection.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn.database"></a>
<ResponseField name="database" kind="property">
The target StarRocks database name.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn.enforce_connection_params"></a>
<ResponseField name="enforce_connection_params" kind="property">
Whether to enforce connection parameters for the StarRocks connection.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn.host"></a>
<ResponseField name="host" kind="property">
The StarRocks FE hostname or IP address.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn.port"></a>
<ResponseField name="port" kind="property">
The MySQL protocol port of the StarRocks FE server.
</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.StarRocksConn.staging"></a>
<ResponseField name="staging" kind="property">
The cloud storage staging configuration (S3Config, AzureConfig, or
GCSConfig).
</ResponseField>

</details>

```python
class StarRocksDest(
```

Bases: DestinationPlugin

Destination plugin for writing data to StarRocks using cloud-staged bulk loading.

Data is first written as Parquet files to the configured cloud storage staging area
(S3, Azure Blob, or GCS) and then ingested into StarRocks via its `FILES()`
table function in an `INSERT INTO … SELECT * FROM FILES(...)` statement.

Bases: [object](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#object)

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.dtypes"></a>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.assert_has_cols"></a>
<ResponseField name="assert_has_cols" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L836">

```python
def assert_has_cols(
    cols: str | list[str],
    exact: bool | None = False,
)
```

Ensures that the (non-system) columns in the TableFrame match the expected
columns.

Raises an exception if the expectation is not met.

If exact is True, the check verifies that the TableFrame contains exactly the
expected columns, with no extra or missing ones.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>> tf.assert_has_cols("a")
>>> tf.assert_has_cols(["a", "b"], exact=True)
```

**Categories:** tableframe

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="cols">
  The expected column name(s). Can be a string or a list of strings.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="exact">
  If True, checks that the TableFrame contains exactly the specified
columns.
</ParamField>

**Raises:** ValueError – If expected columns are missing or unexpected columns are
    present in the TableFrame.

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.cast"></a>
<ResponseField name="cast" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L958">

```python
def cast(
    dtypes: Mapping[td_typing.ColumnNameOrSelector | td_typing.DataType, td_typing.DataType] | td_typing.DataType,
    *,
    strict: bool = True,
)
```

Cast columns to a new data type.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
│ X    ┆ 10   │
│ C    ┆ 3    │
│ D    ┆ 5    │
│ M    ┆ 9    │
│ A    ┆ 100  │
│ M    ┆ 50   │
│ null ┆ 20   │
│ F    ┆ null │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf.cast({"b":td.Float32}).collect()
>>>
┌──────┬───────┐
│ a    ┆ b     │
│ ---  ┆ ---   │
│ str  ┆ f32   │
╞══════╪═══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1.0   │
│ X    ┆ 10.0  │
│ C    ┆ 3.0   │
│ D    ┆ 5.0   │
│ M    ┆ 9.0   │
│ A    ┆ 100.0 │
│ M    ┆ 50.0  │
│ null ┆ 20.0  │
│ F    ┆ null  │
└──────┴───────┘
```

**Categories:** manipulation

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="dtypes">
  Mapping of the column name(s) to the new data type(s).
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="strict">
  If True, raises an error if the cast cannot be performed.
</ParamField>

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.clear"></a>
<ResponseField name="clear" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L1032">

```python
def clear(
    n: int = 0,
)
```

Clears all rows of the TableFrame preserving the schema.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
│ X    ┆ 10   │
│ C    ┆ 3    │
│ D    ┆ 5    │
│ M    ┆ 9    │
│ A    ┆ 100  │
│ M    ┆ 50   │
│ null ┆ 20   │
│ F    ┆ null │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf.cast({"b":td.Float32}).collect()
>>>
┌──────┬───────┐
│ a    ┆ b     │
│ ---  ┆ ---   │
│ str  ┆ f32   │
╞══════╪═══════╡
└──────┴───────┘
```

**Categories:** tableframe

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.drop"></a>
<ResponseField name="drop" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L1596">

```python
def drop(
    *columns: td_typing.ColumnNameOrSelector | Iterable[td_typing.ColumnNameOrSelector],
    strict: bool = True,
)
```

Discard columns from the TableFrame.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ x    ┆ y    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ f64  ┆ f64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ 1.0  ┆ 2.0  │
│ 2.0  ┆ 2.0  │
│ 10.0 ┆ 10.0 │
│ 4.0  ┆ 10.0 │
│ 5.0  ┆ null │
│ null ┆ null │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf.drop("y")
>>>
┌──────┐
│ x    │
│ ---  │
│ f64  │
╞══════╡
│ 1.0  │
│ 2.0  │
│ NaN  │
│ 4.0  │
│ 5.0  │
│ null │
└──────┘
```

**Categories:** projection

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="columns">
  Columns to drop.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="strict">
  If True, raises an error if a column does not exist.
</ParamField>

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.extract_as_columns"></a>
<ResponseField name="extract_as_columns" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2757">

```python
def extract_as_columns(
    offset: int,
    length: int,
)
```

Extract a slice of rows from the table as a column-oriented dictionary.

The result is a mapping of column names to lists of values from the selected
rows.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ a   ┆ b   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ A   ┆ 1   │
│ X   ┆ 10  │
│ C   ┆ 3   │
│ D   ┆ 5   │
│ M   ┆ 9   │
└─────┴─────┘
>>>
>>> tf.extract_as_columns(offset=0, length=2)
    {
        "a": ["A", 1],
        "b": ["X", 10]
    }
```

**Categories:** filters

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="offset" type="int">
  The starting row index of the slice.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="length" type="int">
  The number of rows to include in the slice.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A dictionary where each key is a column name,
and its value is a list of values from the selected slice.

**Returns:** dict[str, list[Any]]

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.extract_as_rows"></a>
<ResponseField name="extract_as_rows" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2704">

```python
def extract_as_rows(
    offset: int,
    length: int,
)
```

Extract a slice of rows from the TableFrame as a list of dictionaries.

Each dictionary represents one row, where keys are column names
and values are the corresponding cell values.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ a   ┆ b   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ A   ┆ 1   │
│ X   ┆ 10  │
│ C   ┆ 3   │
│ D   ┆ 5   │
│ M   ┆ 9   │
└─────┴─────┘
>>>
>>> tf.extract_as_rows(offset=0, length=2)
[
>>>
>>> tf.extract_as_rows(offset=0, length=2)
    [
        {"a": "A", "b": 1},
        {"a": "X", "b": 10},
    ]
```

**Categories:** filters

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="offset" type="int">
  The starting row index of the slice.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="length" type="int">
  The number of rows to include in the slice.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A list of row dictionaries.

**Returns:** list[dict[str, Any]]

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.fill_nan"></a>

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td

┌──────┬──────┐

│ 4.0  ┆ NaN  │
│ 5.0  ┆ null │
│ null ┆ null │
└──────┴──────┘

>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ x    ┆ y    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ f64  ┆ f64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ 1.0  ┆ 2.0  │
│ 2.0  ┆ 2.0  │
│ 10.0 ┆ 10.0 │
│ 4.0  ┆ 10.0 │
│ 5.0  ┆ null │
```

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.filter"></a>
<ResponseField name="filter" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2077">

```python
def filter(
    *predicates: td_typing.IntoExprColumn | Iterable[td_typing.IntoExprColumn] | bool | list[bool] | np.ndarray[Any, Any],
)
```

Filter the TableFrame based on the given predicates.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ a   ┆ b   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ A   ┆ 1   │
│ X   ┆ 10  │
│ C   ┆ 3   │
│ D   ┆ 5   │
│ M   ┆ 9   │
│ A   ┆ 100 │
│ M   ┆ 50  │
└─────┴─────┘
>>>
>>> tf.filter(td.col("a").is_in(["A", "C"]).or_(td.col("b").eq(10)))
>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ a   ┆ b   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ A   ┆ 1   │
│ X   ┆ 10  │
│ C   ┆ 3   │
│ A   ┆ 100 │
└─────┴─────┘
```

**Categories:** filters

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.grok"></a>
<ResponseField name="grok" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2810">

```python
def grok(
    expr: td_typing.IntoExpr,
    pattern: str,
    schema: dict[str, td_col.Column],
)
```

Parse log text into structured fields using a Grok pattern.

Applies a Grok pattern to the given column or expression and directly appends
**one new column per named capture** in the pattern to the output TableFrame.
Rows that do not match the pattern will contain null values for the
extracted columns.

Example

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>> tf = td.TableFrame({"logs": [
...     "alice-login-2023",
...     "bob-logout-2024",
... ]})
>>>
>>> # Capture 3 fields: user, action, year
>>> log_pattern = r"%{WORD:user}-%{WORD:action}-%{INT:year}"
>>> log_schema = {
>>>     "word": td_col.Column("user", td.String),
>>>     "action": td_col.Column("action", td.String),
>>>     "year": td_col.Column("year", td.Int8),
>>> }
>>> out = tf.grok("logs", log_pattern, log_schema)
>>> out.collect()
┌──────────────────┬───────┬────────┬──────┐
│ logs             ┆ user  ┆ action ┆ year │
│ ---              ┆ ---   ┆ ---    ┆ ---  │
│ str              ┆ str   ┆ str    ┆ i64  │
╞══════════════════╪═══════╪════════╪══════╡
│ alice-login-2023 ┆ alice ┆ login  ┆ 2023 │
│ bob-logout-2024  ┆ bob   ┆ logout ┆ 2024 │
└──────────────────┴───────┴────────┴──────┘
```

Notes

- The function automatically expands the Grok captures into separate
columns.
- Non-matching rows will show null for the extracted columns.
- If a pattern defines duplicate capture names, numeric suffixes like
field, field[1] will be used to disambiguate them.

**Categories:** string

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="expr" type="IntoExpr">
  Column name or expression that resolves to a single
string column containing log lines.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="pattern" type="str">
  Grok pattern with named captures (e.g., %&#123;WORD:user&#125;).
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="schema" type="dict">
  A mapping where each capture name
is associated with its corresponding column definition, specifying
both the column name and its data type.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A new TableFrame with one column per Grok capture added.

**Returns:** TableFrame

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.group_by"></a>
<ResponseField name="group_by" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2245">

```python
def group_by(
    *by: td_typing.IntoExpr | Iterable[td_typing.IntoExpr],
)
```

Perform a group by on the TableFrame.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ a   ┆ b   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ A   ┆ 1   │
│ X   ┆ 10  │
│ C   ┆ 3   │
│ D   ┆ 5   │
│ M   ┆ 9   │
│ A   ┆ 100 │
│ M   ┆ 50  │
└─────┴─────┘
>>>
>>> tf.group_by(td.col("a")).agg(td.col("b").sum())
>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ a   ┆ b   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ M   ┆ 59  │
│ A   ┆ 101 │
│ C   ┆ 3   │
│ D   ┆ 5   │
│ X   ┆ 10  │
└─────┴─────┘
```

**Categories:** aggregation

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="by">
  Columns or expressions to group by.
</ParamField>

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.has_cols"></a>
<ResponseField name="has_cols" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L755">

```python
def has_cols(
    cols: str | list[str],
    exact: bool | None = False,
)
```

Verifies the presence of (non-system) columns in the TableFrame.

If exact is True, the check ensures that the TableFrame contains exactly the
specified columns (excluding system columns), with no extras or omissions.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf.has_cols("a")
>>>
(True, {}, {"b"})
>>>
>>> tf.has_cols(["a", "c", "d"])
>>>
(False, {"c", "d"}, {"b"})
>>>
>>> tf.has_cols("a", exact=True)
>>>
(False, {}, {"b"})
>>>
>>> tf.has_cols(["a", "b"], exact=True)
>>>
(True, {}, {})
```

**Categories:** tableframe

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="cols">
  The column name(s) to verify. Can be a string or a list of strings.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="exact">
  If True, checks that the TableFrame contains exactly the specified
columns.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** A boolean indicating whether the check was successful.
A set of columns in cols missing in the TableFrame.
A set of columns in the TableFrame missing in cols.

**Returns:** tuple[bool, set[str], set[str]]

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.has_same_schema"></a>
<ResponseField name="has_same_schema" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L644">

```python
def has_same_schema(
    tf: TableFrame,
)
```

Verifies if the schema of the current TableFrame is same than the provided
TableFrame.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf1: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf2: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ c    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
└──────┴──────┘
>>> tf1.has_same_schema(tf2)
>>>
False
>>>
>>> tf1: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf2: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ str  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
└──────┴──────┘
>>> tf1.has_same_schema(tf2)
>>>
False
```

**Categories:** tableframe

**Categories:** description

**Categories:** description

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="tf">
  The TableFrame to compare with.
</ParamField>

**Returns:** Whether the condition is met or not.

**Returns:** bool

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.is_empty"></a>
<ResponseField name="is_empty" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L715">

```python
def is_empty()
```

Checks if a TableFrame has no rows.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │

>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...

┌──────┬──────┐

╞══════╪══════╡
└──────┴──────┘

True
```

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.item"></a>
<ResponseField name="item" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2670">

```python
def item()
```

Returns a scalar value if the TableFrame contains exactly one user column and
one row.

Raises an exception if there is more than one user column or more than one row.

Returns None if the TableFrame is empty.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌─────┐
│ a   │
│ --- │
│ str │
╞═════╡
│ A   │
└─────┘
>>>
>>> tf.python_version()
>>>
A
```

**Categories:** projection

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.join"></a>
<ResponseField name="join" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L1083">

```python
def join(
    other: TableFrame,
    on: str | Expr | Sequence[str | Expr] | None = None,
    how: Literal['inner', 'left', 'right', 'full', 'semi', 'anti', 'cross', 'outer'] = 'inner',
    *,
    left_on: str | Expr | Sequence[str | Expr] | None = None,
    right_on: str | Expr | Sequence[str | Expr] | None = None,
    suffix: str = '_right',
    join_nulls: bool = False,
    coalesce: bool | None = None,
)
```

Join the TableFrame with another TableFrame.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf1: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
│ X    ┆ 10   │
│ C    ┆ 3    │
│ D    ┆ 5    │
│ M    ┆ 9    │
│ A    ┆ 100  │
│ M    ┆ 50   │
│ null ┆ 20   │
│ F    ┆ null │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf2: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 3    │
│ Y    ┆ 4    │
│ Z    ┆ 5    │
│ A    ┆ 0    │
│ M    ┆ 6    │
│ null ┆ 8    │
│ F    ┆ null │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
An inner join:
>>>
>>> tf1.join(tf2, on="a", how="inner")
>>>
┌─────┬──────┬─────────┐
│ a   ┆ b    ┆ b_right │
│ --- ┆ ---  ┆ ---     │
│ str ┆ i64  ┆ i64     │
╞═════╪══════╪═════════╡
│ A   ┆ 1    ┆ 3       │
│ A   ┆ 1    ┆ 0       │
│ M   ┆ 9    ┆ 6       │
│ A   ┆ 100  ┆ 3       │
│ A   ┆ 100  ┆ 0       │
│ M   ┆ 50   ┆ 6       │
│ F   ┆ null ┆ null    │
└─────┴──────┴─────────┘
>>>
A left join:
>>>
>>> tf1.join(tf2, on="a", how="left")
>>>
┌──────┬──────┬─────────┐
│ a    ┆ b    ┆ b_right │
│ ---  ┆ ---  ┆ ---     │
│ str  ┆ i64  ┆ i64     │
╞══════╪══════╪═════════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    ┆ 3       │
│ A    ┆ 1    ┆ 0       │
│ X    ┆ 10   ┆ null    │
│ C    ┆ 3    ┆ null    │
│ D    ┆ 5    ┆ null    │
│ …    ┆ …    ┆ …       │
│ A    ┆ 100  ┆ 3       │
│ A    ┆ 100  ┆ 0       │
│ M    ┆ 50   ┆ 6       │
│ null ┆ 20   ┆ null    │
│ F    ┆ null ┆ null    │
└──────┴──────┴─────────┘
>>>
Turning off column coalesce:
>>>
>>> tf1.join(tf2, on="a", coalesce=False)
>>>
┌─────┬──────┬─────────┬─────────┐
│ a   ┆ b    ┆ a_right ┆ b_right │
│ --- ┆ ---  ┆ ---     ┆ ---     │
│ str ┆ i64  ┆ str     ┆ i64     │
╞═════╪══════╪═════════╪═════════╡
│ A   ┆ 1    ┆ A       ┆ 3       │
│ A   ┆ 1    ┆ A       ┆ 0       │
│ M   ┆ 9    ┆ M       ┆ 6       │
│ A   ┆ 100  ┆ A       ┆ 3       │
│ A   ┆ 100  ┆ A       ┆ 0       │
│ M   ┆ 50   ┆ M       ┆ 6       │
│ F   ┆ null ┆ F       ┆ null    │
└─────┴──────┴─────────┴─────────┘
```

**Categories:** join

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="other">
  The TableFrame to join.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="on">
  Name(s) of the columns to join on. The column name(s) must be in
both TableFrame’s. Don’t use this parameter if using `left_on
and right_on parameters, or if how=”cross”.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="how">
  Join strategy:

inner: An inner join.
left: A left join.
right: A rigth join.
full: A full join.
cross: The cartesian product.
semi: An inner join but only returning the columns from left
TableFrame.
anti: Rows from the left TableFrame that have no match
in the right TableFrame.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="">
  
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="">
  
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="">
  
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="">
  
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="">
  
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="">
  
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="">
  
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="left_on">
  Name(s) of the columns to join on from the left TableFrame.
It must be used together wit the right_on parameter.
It cannot be used with the on parameter.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="right_on">
  Name(s) of the columns to join on from the right TableFrame.
It must be used together wit the left_on parameter.
It cannot be used with the on parameter.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="suffix">
  Duplicate columns on the right Table are appended this suffix.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="join_nulls">
  If null value matches should produce join rows or not.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="coalesce">
  Collapse join columns into a single column.
</ParamField>

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.last"></a>
<ResponseField name="last" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2496">

```python
def last()
```

Return a TableFrame with the last row.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...

┌─────┬─────┐

│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ A   ┆ 1   │
│ X   ┆ 10  │
│ C   ┆ 3   │
│ D   ┆ 5   │
│ M   ┆ 9   │
└─────┴─────┘
>>>
>>> tf.last()
>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ a   ┆ b   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ M   ┆ 9   │
└─────┴─────┘
```

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.last_row"></a>
<ResponseField name="last_row" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2584">

```python
def last_row(
    named: bool = False,
)
```

Return a tuple or dictionary with the last row, or None if no row.

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ A   ┆ B   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ a   ┆ 1   │
│ b   ┆ 2   │
│ c   ┆ 3   │
└─────┴─────┘
>>>
>>> tf.last_row()
>>>
('c', 3)
>>>
>>> tf.last_row(named=True)
>>>
{'A': 'c', 'B': 3}
```

**Categories:** filters

</ResponseField>

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.rename"></a>

```python
    mapping: dict[str, str],
)
```

Rename columns from the TableFrame.

Examples:

```text

>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ i    ┆ f    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ i32  ┆ f64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ 1    ┆ 3.1  │
│ 2    ┆ 4.1  │
│ 3    ┆ 5.9  │
│ 4    ┆ 2.6  │
│ 5    ┆ 53.5 │
│ 6    ┆ 8.97 │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf.{"i": "index", "f": "amount"})

┌───────┬────────┐
│ index ┆ amount │
│ ----- ┆ ------ │
│ i32   ┆ f64    │
╞═══════╪════════╡
│ 1     ┆ 3.1    │
│ 2     ┆ 4.1    │
│ 3     ┆ 5.9    │
│ 4     ┆ 2.6    │
│ 5     ┆ 53.5   │
│ 6     ┆ 8.97   │
└───────┴────────┘
```

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.select"></a>
<ResponseField name="select" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L2146">

```python
def select(
    *exprs: td_typing.IntoExpr | Iterable[td_typing.IntoExpr],
    **named_exprs: td_typing.IntoExpr,
)
```

Select column(s) from the TableFrame.

Example:

```text

>>>
┌─────┬─────┐
│ a   ┆ b   │
│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │

│ X   ┆ 10  │
│ C   ┆ 3   │
│ D   ┆ 5   │
│ M   ┆ 9   │
│ A   ┆ 100 │
│ M   ┆ 50  │
└─────┴─────┘

│ --- ┆ --- │
│ str ┆ i64 │
╞═════╪═════╡
│ A   ┆ 2   │
│ X   ┆ 20  │
│ C   ┆ 6   │
│ D   ┆ 10  │
│ M   ┆ 18  │
│ A   ┆ 200 │
│ M   ┆ 100 │
└─────┴─────┘
```

<a id="tabsdata.TableFrame.sort"></a>
<ResponseField name="sort" kind="method" source="https://github.com/tabsdata/tabsdata/blob/b1.9/client/platform/src/main/python/tabsdata/tableframe/lazyframe/frame.py#L880">

```python
def sort(
    by: td_typing.IntoExpr | Iterable[td_typing.IntoExpr],
    *more_by: td_typing.IntoExpr,
    descending: bool | Sequence[bool] = False,
    nulls_last: bool | Sequence[bool] = False,
    maintain_order: bool = False,
)
```

Sort the TableFrame by the given column(s) or expression(s).

Example:

```text
>>> import tabsdata as td
>>>
>>> tf: td.TableFrame ...
>>>
┌──────┬──────┐
│ a    ┆ b    │
│ ---  ┆ ---  │
│ str  ┆ i64  │
╞══════╪══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1    │
│ X    ┆ 10   │
│ C    ┆ 3    │
│ D    ┆ 5    │
│ M    ┆ 9    │
│ A    ┆ 100  │
│ M    ┆ 50   │
│ null ┆ 20   │
│ F    ┆ null │
└──────┴──────┘
>>>
>>> tf.sort(td.col("a"), descending = True)
>>>
┌──────┬───────┐
│ a    ┆ b     │
│ ---  ┆ ---   │
│ str  ┆ f32   │
╞══════╪═══════╡
│ A    ┆ 1.0   │
│ X    ┆ 10.0  │
│ C    ┆ 3.0   │
│ D    ┆ 5.0   │
│ M    ┆ 9.0   │
│ A    ┆ 100.0 │
│ M    ┆ 50.0  │
│ null ┆ 20.0  │
│ F    ┆ null  │
└──────┴───────┘
```

**Categories:** tableframe

**Parameters:**

<ParamField path="by">
  Column(s) or expression(s) to sort by.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="more_by">
  Additional colums to sort by.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="descending">
  Specifies if the sorting should be descending or not.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="nulls_last">
  Specifies if null values should be placed last.
</ParamField>

<ParamField path="maintain_order">
  Preserve the order of equal rows.
</ParamField>

</ResponseField>
